## Section 001: Plugin Mcp Integration Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Plugin Mcp Integration Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title names the theme without its governing pipeline, a plugin bundles an MCP server via .mcp.json or an inline mcpServers field, picks one of four transports, and its tools surface under the mcp__plugin_<plugin>_<server>__<tool> prefix
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Plugin Mcp Integration Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the mcp-integration skill states plugins bundle servers in exactly two ways, names stdio, SSE, HTTP, and WebSocket as the supported types, and defines the tool-prefix format that every downstream command must spell out
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Plugin Mcp Integration Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a builder who skips the pipeline hardcodes a server path, picks a transport by habit, then cannot find the tools because the prefixed names were never checked with /mcp
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Plugin Mcp Integration Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference operationalizes MCP server bundling, transport selection, authentication, and tool consumption inside Claude Code plugins, not MCP server implementation itself
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Plugin Mcp Integration Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to open with the two configuration methods, the four transport types, and the tool-naming contract that links server configuration to command frontmatter
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Plugin Mcp Integration Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the whole corpus is a portability argument, ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT} for paths, ${VAR} expansion for secrets, and prefixed tool names all exist so one plugin folder installs cleanly on any machine
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Plugin Mcp Integration Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to start from a dedicated .mcp.json at plugin root, choose stdio for local or bundled servers and SSE for hosted OAuth services, and pre-allow specific prefixed tools in commands
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Plugin Mcp Integration Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the mcp-integration skill states plugins bundle servers in exactly two ways, names stdio, SSE, HTTP, and WebSocket as the supported types, and defines the tool-prefix format that every downstream command must spell out
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Plugin Mcp Integration Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; a builder who skips the pipeline hardcodes a server path, picks a transport by habit, then cannot find the tools because the prefixed names were never checked with /mcp
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Plugin Mcp Integration Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this reference operationalizes MCP server bundling, transport selection, authentication, and tool consumption inside Claude Code plugins, not MCP server implementation itself
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Plugin Mcp Integration Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: open with the two configuration methods, the four transport types, and the tool-naming contract that links server configuration to command frontmatter
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Plugin Mcp Integration Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the whole corpus is a portability argument, ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT} for paths, ${VAR} expansion for secrets, and prefixed tool names all exist so one plugin folder installs cleanly on any machine
### Question 03: When does the default work well?

- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Plugin Mcp Integration Patterns", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because the mcp-integration skill states plugins bundle servers in exactly two ways, names stdio, SSE, HTTP, and WebSocket as the supported types, and defines the tool-prefix format that every downstream command must spell out

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Plugin Mcp Integration Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: a builder who skips the pipeline hardcodes a server path, picks a transport by habit, then cannot find the tools because the prefixed names were never checked with /mcp
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Plugin Mcp Integration Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are MCP servers start when the plugin enables and configuration changes require restarting Claude Code, so mid-session edits to .mcp.json silently do nothing
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Plugin Mcp Integration Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where the plugin runtime performs the documented environment-variable expansion and tool prefixing, both are archive-local contracts until live docs are checked

- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Plugin Mcp Integration Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: shelling out to service CLIs from command hooks, or a standalone user-level MCP configuration outside any plugin

## Section 004: Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed thesis repeats the load-local-first formula instead of the corpus's claim, that external capability should enter a plugin as a bundled MCP server whose transport matches its hosting and whose credentials never live in the configuration
- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the skill's closing workflow prescribes choosing the type first, using ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT} for all references, documenting environment variables, and letting OAuth or env-var expansion carry every secret
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a thesis built on configuration mechanics alone would bless a working integration that leaks its token the first time the plugin is pushed to git
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the thesis orients use of this reference and does not compress the per-transport rules it stands on
- **revision_decision:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to restate the combined inference as bundle the server with the plugin, match transport to hosting, keep secrets in the environment, and expose the fewest prefixed tools each command needs
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the thesis is a separation of custody, the plugin owns configuration shape, the user's shell owns secrets, and Claude Code owns OAuth tokens, so no party ever holds all three

- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 10 on second-order deductions: that deduction follows from the skill's closing workflow prescribes choosing the type first, using ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT} for all references, documenting environment variables, and letting OAuth or env-var expansion carry every secret
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 10 on second-order deductions: its reach is limited where a thesis built on configuration mechanics alone would bless a working integration that leaks its token the first time the plugin is pushed to git
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 10 on second-order deductions: carry the deduction forward only within the thesis orients use of this reference and does not compress the per-transport rules it stands on
- **revision_decision:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 10 on second-order deductions: change the guidance by applying this concrete revision: restate the combined inference as bundle the server with the plugin, match transport to hosting, keep secrets in the environment, and expose the fewest prefixed tools each command needs
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: a latency-first thesis that favors stdio everywhere, or a zero-trust thesis that wraps every service in an mTLS stdio proxy This changes how the section resolves what single claim should orient a builder integrating an external service.

- **supporting_reason:** Section 006 "External Research Source Map", Question 10 on second-order deductions: that deduction follows from the skill names https://modelcontextprotocol.io/ and https://docs.claude.com/en/docs/claude-code/mcp as official docs, and none of the mapped or cited URLs was retrieved during this evolution
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 006 "External Research Source Map", Question 10 on second-order deductions: its reach is limited where a refresh cycle following the seed map would poll a dated resources spec page while transport options, auth flows, and the tool-prefix format drift unwatched
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 006 "External Research Source Map", Question 10 on second-order deductions: carry the deduction forward only within the map governs external freshness checks for this theme and does not vouch for any URL's current content
- **revision_decision:** Section 006 "External Research Source Map", Question 10 on second-order deductions: change the guidance by applying this concrete revision: flag all listed URLs as unretrieved candidates, deduplicate the doubled rows, and record the Claude Code MCP docs as the missing primary anchor for future refresh
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 006 "External Research Source Map", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: drop the duplicated rows, or keep them with an explicit dedup note and a spec-version column This changes how the section resolves which external sources deserve retrieval when this reference is refreshed.

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 10 on second-order deductions: its reach is limited where a plugin passing only the document verifier can still fail at first use because no gate ever confirmed the server connects or the tools appear
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 10 on second-order deductions: carry the deduction forward only within the gates prove this reference and its integrations are checkable, they do not replace the external service's own test environment
- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 10 on second-order deductions: change the guidance by applying this concrete revision: add the corpus loop, /mcp for server and tool visibility, claude --debug for connection attempts, discovery logs, auth flows, and tool errors, and the seven-item validation checklist
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: curl the health endpoint with the Bearer token as authentication.md shows, or script the checklist into CI This changes how the section resolves which commands must pass before an integration change is trusted.

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guide says when to open this reference but not the corpus's sharpest agent rule, commands must pre-allow each prefixed MCP tool in frontmatter while agents may use any tool autonomously without pre-approval
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because tool-usage.md states agents have broader tool access than commands, can use any tool Claude determines necessary, and need no pre-allowed lists, while commands enumerate tools or use a sparing wildcard
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: an author applying command rules to agents writes pointless allowlists, and one applying agent freedom to commands ships tools that silently cannot run
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide routes usage of this reference and the exposure decision between commands and agents, not agent architecture at large
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the exposure fork, wrap user-interactive validated calls in commands with named tools, give autonomous multi-step workflows to agents that document which tools they typically use
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the fork is a permission gradient, commands trade flexibility for reviewable least privilege while agents trade reviewability for autonomy, which is why tool-usage still asks agents to document their typical tools
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to expose single validated operations as commands with named tools and reserve agents for workflows that chain queries, analysis, and writes
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because tool-usage.md states agents have broader tool access than commands, can use any tool Claude determines necessary, and need no pre-allowed lists, while commands enumerate tools or use a sparing wildcard

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the guide routes usage of this reference and the exposure decision between commands and agents, not agent architecture at large
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add the exposure fork, wrap user-interactive validated calls in commands with named tools, give autonomous multi-step workflows to agents that document which tools they typically use
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the fork is a permission gradient, commands trade flexibility for reviewable least privilege while agents trade reviewability for autonomy, which is why tool-usage still asks agents to document their typical tools

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guide weighs adopt, adapt, avoid without the corpus's central tradeoff table, stdio versus SSE versus HTTP versus WebSocket across transport, state, auth, latency, and reconnection
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because server-types.md closes with a comparison matrix and a choosing-the-right-type section that assigns each transport its use cases and costs
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: transport chosen by familiarity ships WebSocket complexity for a stateless REST backend or stdio for a service that needs OAuth
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide covers transport and adoption tradeoffs for this theme, not service-side architecture
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the four-way fork, stdio for local lowest-latency stateful tools, SSE for hosted OAuth services with automatic reconnection, HTTP for stateless token-auth request-response, WebSocket for real-time bidirectional streaming
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the matrix is really two questions, where does the process run and who holds the connection state, answer both and the transport falls out without reading the marketing names
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to stdio when the plugin ships the server, SSE when a vendor hosts it, HTTP when wrapping a REST API, WebSocket only when latency or push justifies persistent connections
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because server-types.md closes with a comparison matrix and a choosing-the-right-type section that assigns each transport its use cases and costs
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; transport chosen by familiarity ships WebSocket complexity for a stateless REST backend or stdio for a service that needs OAuth
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the guide covers transport and adoption tradeoffs for this theme, not service-side architecture
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add the four-way fork, stdio for local lowest-latency stateful tools, SSE for hosted OAuth services with automatic reconnection, HTTP for stateless token-auth request-response, WebSocket for real-time bidirectional streaming
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the matrix is really two questions, where does the process run and who holds the connection state, answer both and the transport falls out without reading the marketing names

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?

## Section 012: Local Corpus Hierarchy
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed hierarchy marks the archive skill canonical and everything else supporting without noting the live claude-skills copies are byte-identical duplicates, making the duplicate role, not supporting context, their accurate label
- **supporting_reason:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because diff comparisons during this evolution showed each claude-skills file identical to its archive counterpart, and the seed's own vocabulary includes a duplicate role it never assigns
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a reviewer following the seed labels would treat the live SKILL.md as independent supporting context and cite it as corroboration
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the hierarchy assigns evidential weight within this theme's eight rows, not across the repository
- **revision_decision:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to keep the archive skill canonical, keep its three reference files supporting, and relabel the four live copies as duplicates pending divergence
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the hierarchy inverts on drift, the moment a live copy diverges it stops being a duplicate and becomes the canonical row because it reflects current skill behavior

## Section 013: Theme Specific Artifact
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed artifact names a resource/tool boundary map without the concrete columns the corpus supplies, server name, transport type, auth method, env vars required, tools exposed, and commands pre-allowing them
- **supporting_reason:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because every corpus example carries exactly those fields, .mcp.json declares server and transport, authentication.md declares the credential route, tool-usage.md declares prefixed names and allowlists
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a boundary map without the env-var column cannot answer the first setup question a new user asks, what must I export before this works
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the artifact documents one plugin's integration surface for review and onboarding, not the external service's API
- **revision_decision:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to complete the artifact as a per-server table, name, transport, auth method, required environment variables, exposed tool names, and the commands or agents consuming each
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the artifact is the README the corpus keeps demanding, three separate files order authors to document required environment variables, and this table is that documentation in reviewable form
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to fill the table from .mcp.json and command frontmatter before publishing, and regenerate it on every configuration change

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed model bounds source counts without the corpus's operational load shape, one plugin may run multiple servers of mixed types, each contributing ten-plus tools that commands and agents fan out across
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the skill's key capabilities promise ten-plus related tools per service and both the skill and server-types show multi-server plugins mixing stdio, SSE, and HTTP
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a model assuming one server and a handful of tools underestimates allowlist sprawl and debug surface the moment a second service joins
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the model sizes integration work per plugin, not external service capacity
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to model workload as servers times transports times tools, with lazy connection on first use and batching as the pressure valves the corpus provides
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that lazy loading shifts cost from startup to first call, so perceived tool latency includes connection setup exactly once, a spike the corpus says is managed automatically but authors should expect
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to bound each plugin to the services one workflow needs, and batch filtered queries instead of per-item calls as both performance sections instruct
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the skill's key capabilities promise ten-plus related tools per service and both the skill and server-types show multi-server plugins mixing stdio, SSE, and HTTP

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the model sizes integration work per plugin, not external service capacity
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: model workload as servers times transports times tools, with lazy connection on first use and batching as the pressure valves the corpus provides

## Section 019: Reliability Target
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed targets track evidence hygiene without the corpus's reliability posture, automatic reconnection for SSE and WebSocket, retry with a bounded cap for tool calls, and graceful degradation with user-facing remediation
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because server-types assigns automatic reconnection to SSE and WebSocket and process respawn to stdio, and tool-usage's error pattern caps retries at three attempts before informing the user
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: an integration without the bounded retry turns a transient 429 into either an infinite loop or an immediate user-facing failure
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: targets cover the plugin-side integration path, the external service's own SLA is out of scope
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to set targets as reconnection handled by transport, tool retries capped at three, every failure path ending in a remediation message naming what the user should check
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the corpus's reliability chain has three layers with distinct owners, transport reconnection belongs to Claude Code, retry policy to the command author, and remediation text to the UX, so a gap analysis checks each owner separately
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to rely on transport reconnection, implement the three-attempt retry only for retryable errors, and template the error messages on the corpus's checklist form
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because server-types assigns automatic reconnection to SSE and WebSocket and process respawn to stdio, and tool-usage's error pattern caps retries at three attempts before informing the user
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; an integration without the bounded retry turns a transient 429 into either an infinite loop or an immediate user-facing failure
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: targets cover the plugin-side integration path, the external service's own SLA is out of scope
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: set targets as reconnection handled by transport, tool retries capped at three, every failure path ending in a remediation message naming what the user should check
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the corpus's reliability chain has three layers with distinct owners, transport reconnection belongs to Claude Code, retry policy to the command author, and remediation text to the UX, so a gap analysis checks each owner separately
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: error types are classified first, auth failures must not be retried like rate limits
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because server-types assigns automatic reconnection to SSE and WebSocket and process respawn to stdio, and tool-usage's error pattern caps retries at three attempts before informing the user
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the success case ends where an integration without the bounded retry turns a transient 429 into either an infinite loop or an immediate user-facing failure
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: treat these operating conditions as bounded by targets cover the plugin-side integration path, the external service's own SLA is out of scope
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: add an explicit use-when statement grounded in error types are classified first, auth failures must not be retried like rate limits
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: show the second-order benefit that the corpus's reliability chain has three layers with distinct owners, transport reconnection belongs to Claude Code, retry policy to the command author, and remediation text to the UX, so a gap analysis checks each owner separately
### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: an integration without the bounded retry turns a transient 429 into either an infinite loop or an immediate user-facing failure
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are stdio has no reconnection, only process respawn, so a crashing local server needs its own crash-handling per server-types best practices
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where error types are classified first, auth failures must not be retried like rate limits
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 04 on failure boundary: distinguish a genuine failure from an out-of-scope case using targets cover the plugin-side integration path, the external service's own SLA is out of scope
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: circuit breakers above the retry cap, or health probes before workflows that chain many calls
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 04 on failure boundary: retain uncertainty explicitly: reconnection backoff timing is undocumented in the archive
### Question 05: Which alternatives and tradeoffs matter?

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because SKILL.md's common-issues section defines all three signatures and their checks, URL and process for connection, /mcp and exact names for tools, cached tokens and scopes for auth
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: an operator without the signatures debugs by restart superstition instead of walking the documented checks
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the table catalogs plugin-side integration failures, service-side outages appear only as their connection symptoms

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guidance classifies verification failures without the corpus's call-level policy, classify the error first, retry transient failures at most three times, respect rate limits, and batch to avoid provoking them
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because tool-usage's error-handling pattern waits and retries with a three-attempt maximum, its 429 row demands rate-limit handling, and both performance sections prescribe batching as the load reducer
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: unclassified retries hammer a rate-limited service harder, converting a soft 429 into sustained throttling
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guidance governs plugin-side tool calls, server-side throttling policy belongs to the service
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to adopt classify-then-retry with the three-attempt cap, treat 429 as a signal to slow and batch, and treat auth and validation errors as non-retryable
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that batching is preemptive backpressure, the corpus's single-filtered-query rule removes the call volume that makes retry policy matter in the first place
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to batch first, retry transient failures up to three times with waits, and surface everything else with remediation text
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because tool-usage's error-handling pattern waits and retries with a three-attempt maximum, its 429 row demands rate-limit handling, and both performance sections prescribe batching as the load reducer
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; unclassified retries hammer a rate-limited service harder, converting a soft 429 into sustained throttling
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the guidance governs plugin-side tool calls, server-side throttling policy belongs to the service
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: adopt classify-then-retry with the three-attempt cap, treat 429 as a signal to slow and batch, and treat auth and validation errors as non-retryable
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies batching is preemptive backpressure, the corpus's single-filtered-query rule removes the call volume that makes retry policy matter in the first place
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: error responses distinguish transient from permanent causes, opaque errors must be treated as permanent after one retry
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because tool-usage's error-handling pattern waits and retries with a three-attempt maximum, its 429 row demands rate-limit handling, and both performance sections prescribe batching as the load reducer
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the success case ends where unclassified retries hammer a rate-limited service harder, converting a soft 429 into sustained throttling
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: treat these operating conditions as bounded by the guidance governs plugin-side tool calls, server-side throttling policy belongs to the service
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: add an explicit use-when statement grounded in error responses distinguish transient from permanent causes, opaque errors must be treated as permanent after one retry
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: show the second-order benefit that batching is preemptive backpressure, the corpus's single-filtered-query rule removes the call volume that makes retry policy matter in the first place
### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: unclassified retries hammer a rate-limited service harder, converting a soft 429 into sustained throttling
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are partial batch success needs its own report shape, the corpus's eight-of-ten summary with named failures, not a blanket retry of the whole batch
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: crossing one boundary does not invalidate the default where error responses distinguish transient from permanent causes, opaque errors must be treated as permanent after one retry
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: distinguish a genuine failure from an out-of-scope case using the guidance governs plugin-side tool calls, server-side throttling policy belongs to the service
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: prescribe this bounded recovery instead of forcing the default: exponential backoff beyond the flat wait, or queueing writes through the MCP server when it offers bulk endpoints
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 04 on failure boundary: retain uncertainty explicitly: wait durations between retries are unspecified in the archive
### Question 05: Which alternatives and tradeoffs matter?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 05 on alternatives and tradeoffs: the meaningful alternatives are these: exponential backoff beyond the flat wait, or queueing writes through the MCP server when it offers bulk endpoints

- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: the highest-value warnings are partial batch success needs its own report shape, the corpus's eight-of-ten summary with named failures, not a blanket retry of the whole batch

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: do not classify ordinary variation as failure when error responses distinguish transient from permanent causes, opaque errors must be treated as permanent after one retry

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed checklist audits document reviews without the corpus's observability surfaces, /mcp for server and tool inventory, claude --debug for connection, discovery, auth, and call errors, and stderr-only logging for stdio servers
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the debugging sections direct authors to debug logs for four named signal classes, and server-types insists stdio servers log to stderr because stdout carries the protocol
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a stdio server that logs to stdout corrupts its own JSON-RPC channel, the observability mistake that breaks the thing observed
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the checklist covers plugin-side observability, service-side dashboards are out of scope
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to adopt the three surfaces as the checklist, inventory via /mcp, flows via debug logs, server internals via stderr, each mapped to the failure stage it illuminates

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed method verifies document quality without the corpus's performance levers, batch filtered queries over per-item calls, cache expensive results for reuse, and parallelize independent tool calls
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because both performance sections show the same before-after query shape, and tool-usage adds caching and parallel calls as the remaining levers
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a workflow looping get_task over fifty IDs performs fifty round trips where one filtered search with a limit would do
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the method verifies plugin-side call efficiency, server-side query optimization is out of scope
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to verify by inspecting workflows for the three levers, filters with limits on searches, cached reuse of expensive results, and parallel calls only for independent operations

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed statement bounds reference usage without the corpus's scale edges, stdio dies with the session, HTTP is stateless per request, WebSocket holds persistent connections, and mTLS enterprise auth needs a stdio wrapper workaround
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because server-types assigns each transport its state model, and authentication.md states mTLS is not directly supported, prescribing the wrapper as the boundary-crossing device
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: pushing session-lifetime stdio into always-on service duty or stateless HTTP into streaming duty fails at the transport's designed edge, not from bugs
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the statement bounds plugin-side integration scale, service capacity planning is external
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the edges per transport, session-bound stdio, stateless HTTP, connection-holding WebSocket with heartbeat and buffering duties, and wrapper-mediated enterprise auth
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the wrapper workaround generalizes, any capability the MCP configuration cannot express, mTLS, custom signing, exotic transports, moves into a stdio server the plugin ships, making stdio the escape hatch at every boundary
